  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_70df41db-e18b-42cb-84b2-aaacdd060a9b'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer1644717586015761226">Ethan lives a secret life as a Guardian of the Named. Under the guidance of Arkarian, his mentor, and with the help of Isabel, his unlikely but highly capable apprentice, Ethan has become a valued member of this other-worldly corps. As the only defense against the evil Order of Chaos, the Named travel through time to prevent the Order from altering history and thereby gain</span>
  <span id="freeText1644717586015761226" style="display:none">Ethan lives a secret life as a Guardian of the Named. Under the guidance of Arkarian, his mentor, and with the help of Isabel, his unlikely but highly capable apprentice, Ethan has become a valued member of this other-worldly corps. As the only defense against the evil Order of Chaos, the Named travel through time to prevent the Order from altering history and thereby gaining power in the present and the future.<br /><br />As the threat from the Order intensifies, secrets of the past are revealed and villains and heroes are exposed. This gripping fantasy is set in modern times, but is infused with intrigue from the past, super-natural characters and surprising plot twists. Curley has written a winner through to the end.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer715850813792045117">Reread August 2 to 7, 2015 for #fivefaves<br/><br/>Maybe more of a 3.5/5 stars. NOT SURE.<br/>Well I still really liked this book, but I'm not sure if I can count it in one of my faves anymore. I still really love the story and overall concept - they are so unique and wonderful that it's hard NOT to love them. However the writing is so SO bad. It's something I definitely wouldn't have noticed as much years ago, but it's really bad. The character development is definitely lacking as well, and the characters bei</span>
  <span id="freeText715850813792045117" style="display:none">Reread August 2 to 7, 2015 for #fivefaves<br /><br />Maybe more of a 3.5/5 stars. NOT SURE.<br />Well I still really liked this book, but I'm not sure if I can count it in one of my faves anymore. I still really love the story and overall concept - they are so unique and wonderful that it's hard NOT to love them. However the writing is so SO bad. It's something I definitely wouldn't have noticed as much years ago, but it's really bad. The character development is definitely lacking as well, and the characters being SO YOUNG (aka not 18) kinda makes things like romances a little icky. SO I STILL LIKED IT but I now have more issues with it. At least now I recognize them!</span>

<div id="review_453762842" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/453762842" />
    <a title="Allison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9371994-allison"><img alt="Allison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461856985p2/9371994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/453762842?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison" href="/user/show/9371994-allison">Allison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781599908823" href="/book/show/12849238-the-named">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=romance-rating-mild-g-pg">romance-rating-mild-g-pg</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=series-i-finished">series-i-finished</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=published-2000s">published-2000s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=series-complete">series-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=own-ebook">own-ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=romantic-elements">romantic-elements</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer453762842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer692835717635634243"><br/>The first half of this book was just like all the other YA paranormals that I’ve grown so tired of - teenagers in class, passing notes, grumpy teachers, girl & boy working together, one with a crush on the other. Depressing home lives, parent and sibling issues, blah blah. Not a lot actually happens at first, but I could see where it was going and was quickly falling into eye-rolling mode, fighting boredom and frustration. How many times have I seen these clichés play out by now?<br/><br/>When I picked th</span>
  <span id="freeText692835717635634243" style="display:none"><br />The first half of this book was just like all the other YA paranormals that I’ve grown so tired of - teenagers in class, passing notes, grumpy teachers, girl &amp; boy working together, one with a crush on the other. Depressing home lives, parent and sibling issues, blah blah. Not a lot actually happens at first, but I could see where it was going and was quickly falling into eye-rolling mode, fighting boredom and frustration. How many times have I seen these clichés play out by now?<br /><br />When I picked this up, I really thought it would be more about time travel adventures. Although the Named are guardians of the timeline, this story is more about the guardians in the present than what they do when they travel to the past. The teenagers are in training (very vaguely described aside from repeated mention of parent and sibling problems caused by the two spending time together), and the focus is not enough on their lives as guardians, at least at first. Irritated at being sucked into another one of these sorts of books, I forced myself onward, prepared to skim if necessary to finish this thing. <br /><br />Then something changed. I’m not sure exactly when I stopped having to force myself to read. Probably about the time high school dropped out of it and we actually got past the training and into the missions (yes, this does happen!). Then there were a couple small events that challenged my sense of knowing exactly where it was going, and then stuff started happening and I got interested and then - then the end. Just as it started to get up to speed, it ended, and now I’m going to have to read the next one. I sincerely hope I don’t have to wait through another half book of the daily lives of teenagers before things get interesting again. Please no more high school. If we can stick to the business of the Named, I’ll be happy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="692835717635634243" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Elica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5939516-elica"><img alt="Elica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579006060p2/5939516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer193193678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16908505789809196755">Very adventurous, a definite page turner.<br/><br/>It had me wanting more after each chapter, i literally could not put this book down.<br/><br/>The characters are a fine set all with their own personality.<br/><br/><br/><br/>My only complaint is that they were not defined much, as in, i had no idea how they looked like. At times Curley would describe a few of their qualities, but not enough to get a strong image. <br/><br/><br/><br/>If anything, all i got a good image of was when they turned into someone else. Arkarian is my favorite character along wit</span>
  <span id="freeText16908505789809196755" style="display:none">Very adventurous, a definite page turner.<br /><br />It had me wanting more after each chapter, i literally could not put this book down.<br /><br />The characters are a fine set all with their own personality.<br /><br /><br /><br />My only complaint is that they were not defined much, as in, i had no idea how they looked like. At times Curley would describe a few of their qualities, but not enough to get a strong image. <br /><br /><br /><br />If anything, all i got a good image of was when they turned into someone else. Arkarian is my favorite character along with the intelligent Isabel.<br /><br />I'm glad this book is a series.<br /><br /><br /><br />Recommended!<br /><br />Man twists and turns, and at times it seems predictable, but goes back to being "What the?"<br /><br /><br /><br />thankfully it isn't another book about werewolves and vampires, in fact, hardly any love is in this book!<br /><br />Mostly action and world traveling.<br /><br />It's a very good read, and i do hope a very good series.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer453639207118712468">So I finished the book and I certainly enjoyed the time that I was reading it, but I feel that this only deserves 3 stars because anything higher should be reserved for particularly good work. This was candy. <br/><br/>But the candy tasted a little bitter because with such an intriguiging concept, the execution was a bit of a disappointment. There could have been so many interesting theames explored with the idea of how tightly interwoven events in space-time are. But it often seemed like the timetravel a</span>
  <span id="freeText453639207118712468" style="display:none">So I finished the book and I certainly enjoyed the time that I was reading it, but I feel that this only deserves 3 stars because anything higher should be reserved for particularly good work. This was candy. <br /><br />But the candy tasted a little bitter because with such an intriguiging concept, the execution was a bit of a disappointment. There could have been so many interesting theames explored with the idea of how tightly interwoven events in space-time are. But it often seemed like the timetravel aspect was just a vessle used to chug the story along to the end. And this wouldn't be such a problem if it felt like that end had any sort of purpose at all. But this is a story that exists just to exist. <br /><br />On the positive side I will say that I liked the central characters Isabel, Ethan, and Arkarian which is a plus. And I actually liked the shifting of perspectives because I enjoyed hearing from both Isabel and Ethan.<br /><br />In the end though, there's just so much more that could have been done with the plot and characters which is why I'm so frustrated that it only ended up being a fun read.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_980523815" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/980523815" />
    <a title="snowplum" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29859477-snowplum"><img alt="snowplum" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443774075p2/29859477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/980523815?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="snowplum" class="user" itemprop="url" name="snowplum" href="/user/show/29859477-snowplum">snowplum</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer980523815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9030275197265090857">This book is the literary equivalent of Chinese food. You really enjoy it sometimes, you share it with friends who enjoy it too, and an hour later you forget it because it didn't really <i>satisfy</i> you in some fundamental way. <br/><br/>The better attributes of the book are the greater-than-average number of ideas included in the plot and the fantasy elements. Interesting choices of destinations in time and historical figures to meet (not the obvious choices) set the book apart right away. Then the descriptio</span>
  <span id="freeText9030275197265090857" style="display:none">This book is the literary equivalent of Chinese food. You really enjoy it sometimes, you share it with friends who enjoy it too, and an hour later you forget it because it didn't really <i>satisfy</i> you in some fundamental way. <br /><br />The better attributes of the book are the greater-than-average number of ideas included in the plot and the fantasy elements. Interesting choices of destinations in time and historical figures to meet (not the obvious choices) set the book apart right away. Then the description of the catacombs or chambers between worlds with their magic puzzles and traps takes the book to a cool fantasy place for a while. <br /><br />The weakest attribute of the book is the shifting perspective. It feels VERY short attention span to go back and forth between Ethan and Isabelle so often. This relates to the other major problem, which is anything that pertains to a character other than Ethan or Isabelle. Because Curley already has her hands full trying to flesh out two characters in a first-person way (which requires a lot more dextrous writing than having multiple main characters in third person omniscient), she just has nothing left to give the characters who aren't given a first-person voice. Arkarian, Matt, and Rochelle are all little more than sketches, which is disappointing when you find out that they are going to be much more important in the later books. <br /><br />I also don't think Curley does very well at giving Ethan and Isabelle distinct voices -- there's virtually nothing about the way they speak that differentiates gender, intelligence, priorities, interests, influences... and Curley misses almost any opportunity to have them think/see/notice different things about the secondary characters, which might differentiate Ethan and Isabelle better and give you more insight into the people they know. Also gotta say, Ethan is pretty smooth around the edges for a teenage boy, which starts to seem implausible the more seriously you try to take the book.<br /><br />So, all in all, The Named is a lot like Chinese food among friends. You get to sample a lot of different things, some of which are pretty tasty and some of which are just variety for variety's sake. You have a nice, chill time. And soon after you put it away, you're hungry again. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9030275197265090857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review980523815">

<div id="review_61223831" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/61223831" />
    <a title="Victoria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2299764-victoria"><img alt="Victoria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242771111p2/2299764.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/61223831?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/2299764-victoria">Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61223831" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6624203439419396451">I was really excited about this book...it got such a high rating and seemed like such a fantastic premise. Maybe that's why it seemed to fall short. <br/><br/>Ethan is a Guardian of Time; he travels to the past in order to keep evil denizens from the Order of Chaos from changing it, thus affecting the future. Of course Ethan's only a teenager, but he's already very good at what he does. So the Guard decides to test him by giving him the willful Isabel as his new apprentice. But Isabel's initiation brings </span>
  <span id="freeText6624203439419396451" style="display:none">I was really excited about this book...it got such a high rating and seemed like such a fantastic premise. Maybe that's why it seemed to fall short. <br /><br />Ethan is a Guardian of Time; he travels to the past in order to keep evil denizens from the Order of Chaos from changing it, thus affecting the future. Of course Ethan's only a teenager, but he's already very good at what he does. So the Guard decides to test him by giving him the willful Isabel as his new apprentice. But Isabel's initiation brings a whole host of problems to the surface, most of them revolving around an ancient prophecy.<br /><br />It sounds so wonderful, and <i>so</i> much could have been done with such a concept. Which is why it comes so close to painful to watch the story enacted quite a bit below its potential.<br /><br />In fact, I think my irritation with this novel stems from the wasted potential. It was enjoyable on some levels, but all I could think was how much better it could have been. Ethan and Isabel have all the seeds of great characters, as do others they interact with; Ethan's wise and ever-youthful mentor Arkarian probably comes closest to being a truly relatable person. But again, they never come to life; they remain flat and stiffly-written, shifting between easy teenage narration and speech too stilted to ever really come out of a mouth. I think this is partly due to the first person narration, something that most authors are either good at...or aren't. Curley unfortunately is not. The emotions are also only vaguely felt.<br /><br />The story itself also grazes shallowly along the surface of its awesome premise. Plot bumps detract from the realism; it's too obvious how the author hand-waves the various parts of the Guard with magic, illusions, or mysterious powers. It's also a tad misleading; I was expecting the bulk of the story to involve the time traveling missions, but by the end more focus is put on old feuds with evil Chaos denizens then on anything historical. And the few missions sprinkled in do little to actually expose the reader to the time period, barreling through the process and tossing in some random historical figures like King Richard II and Abigail Adams.<br /><br />The premise saves the story, giving it some decent moments and a pretty good climax and conclusion. I'm not sure I'll be reading the rest of the trilogy right away; it didn't reel me in as I'd hoped it would.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6624203439419396451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16863412347009215003">Let me just say that I was sooo impatient to start this series of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/60478.Marianne_Curley' title='Marianne Curley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Marianne Curley</a>! After reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/565595.Old_Magic' title='Old Magic by Marianne Curley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Old Magic</a> as a teenager and loved it, I searched for the Guardians of Time for many years unitll I could eventually find them on an e-book format since it never was translated in Greek.<br/><br/>The Νamed is a fast paced YA story, only the beginning of 4 books really. It made me remembered of Old magic (which I've read countless of times over the years), and a little of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2265776.Ruby_Red' title='Ruby Red by Linzi Glass' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ruby Red</a>.   <span id="freeText16863412347009215003" style="display:none">Let me just say that I was sooo impatient to start this series of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/60478.Marianne_Curley" title="Marianne Curley" rel="nofollow noopener">Marianne Curley</a>! After reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/565595.Old_Magic" title="Old Magic by Marianne Curley" rel="nofollow noopener">Old Magic</a> as a teenager and loved it, I searched for the Guardians of Time for many years unitll I could eventually find them on an e-book format since it never was translated in Greek.<br /><br />The Νamed is a fast paced YA story, only the beginning of 4 books really. It made me remembered of Old magic (which I've read countless of times over the years), and a little of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2265776.Ruby_Red" title="Ruby Red by Linzi Glass" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruby Red</a>. Yes, it contains time travel but in a way that combines adventure, hope and love.<br /><br /><b>I was afraid that since it was written 14 years ago, it might not be such a surprise, the plot twists might me old fashiond, like the story. Well... I'm happy to tell you that this is not the case!</b> It might be my happy feeling of finally reading it, but it didn't dissapoint. I might given it 4 stars since there was some minor things that I didn't like, but in the end, the familiar feeling of reading a Marianne Curley's book, along with the story and the warmth in my heart now that I've finish it, I know that there is no alternative. This is a five star book for me and I cannot wait to read the next on the series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30805751.The_Dark" title="The Dark by Marianne Curley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dark</a>.<br /><br /><b>To all my friends:</b> since I know that our tastes are alike, mark this as "want to read" and download it when you're feeling like you want a fast paced YA, sweet, adventurous and (even though some times predictable), with many potentional for the next 3 books of the series!<br /><br />PS. Also, after the Darkling, I think I'm in love again 😍😍😍</span>

<div id="review_154010025" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154010025" />
    <a title="Momo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5119056-momo"><img alt="Momo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504526373p2/5119056.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154010025?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Momo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Momo" href="/user/show/5119056-momo">Momo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781599905433" href="/book/show/7430223-the-named">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154010025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3692937239703195960">I will have to say that I was pretty disappointed with this book. The back cover promised to portray a story of excitement and romance which was quite misleading. The premise of the story was excellent, but the delivery was flat. The characters are not fully developed and the connections between characters are also not explored to satisfaction. Time travel isn’t real, and the author did a good job of remind me of that while reading. None of it seemed to transcend reality: the characters, plot, e</span>
  <span id="freeText3692937239703195960" style="display:none">I will have to say that I was pretty disappointed with this book. The back cover promised to portray a story of excitement and romance which was quite misleading. The premise of the story was excellent, but the delivery was flat. The characters are not fully developed and the connections between characters are also not explored to satisfaction. Time travel isn’t real, and the author did a good job of remind me of that while reading. None of it seemed to transcend reality: the characters, plot, events, even dialogue. All of it seemed faked.<br /> <br />Curley has two different main characters (Ethan and Isabel). Time is spent on both stories within the book and because of this neither character is fully understood. I didn’t care too much about them or their well-being because while reading the book, I was fully aware that this was a story, and that these characters were fictitious beings. The characters came to epiphany-style realizations far too often. I found myself thinking, “Really? You just figured all of that out by looking at the rock?” It didn’t make sense as to why things just happened to make sense to the characters. On top of it all, the reactions to events were typically atypical of a normal (real) person. Inconsistency also played a large role in my dislike of this book, not to mention predictability. I found myself trying to force myself to finish the book, if only to confirm the ending that I had already figured out on my own.<br /><br />In the end, I gave this book a 2.5 star rating. It was not the worst book I’ve ever read but I didn’t really enjoy it. I can’t say whether or not I’ll be reading the final two books in this series. I’ll have to take a little break and see if I’m still curious enough about the ending to continue on. As of right now, I think I’ve had enough of The Named for a little while.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3692937239703195960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2349311697" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2349311697" />
    <a title="Saimi Korhonen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59275887-saimi-korhonen"><img alt="Saimi Korhonen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561832552p2/59275887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2349311697?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Saimi Korhonen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Saimi Korhonen" href="/user/show/59275887-saimi-korhonen">Saimi Korhonen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59275887-saimi-korhonen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2349311697" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11251340234963535211"><i> "I want to take you to a place where it is midnight every day and black irises glisten under a bleeding moon." </i><br/><br/>This trilogy has been a favorite of mine ever since I was a wee kid, and every time I re-read it I'm just filled with nostalgia, love and happiness. It's not a perfect book (there's a lot of insta-love and all that), but it still holds up. I love it. So, The Named begins The Guardians of Time trilogy that follows a group of people with magical abilities whose main task in life is to pr</span>
  <span id="freeText11251340234963535211" style="display:none"><i> "I want to take you to a place where it is midnight every day and black irises glisten under a bleeding moon." </i><br /><br />This trilogy has been a favorite of mine ever since I was a wee kid, and every time I re-read it I'm just filled with nostalgia, love and happiness. It's not a perfect book (there's a lot of insta-love and all that), but it still holds up. I love it. So, The Named begins The Guardians of Time trilogy that follows a group of people with magical abilities whose main task in life is to protect history from those who would seek to alter it. These people travel back in time to make sure that history progresses as it should, because the villains, led by an immortal Goddess, are determined to change history to change the present. It's such an interesting premise and magic system - I love all the different abilities these characters have and I love reading about their missions into the past. <br /><br />The characters are incredibly dear to me. The Named is narrated by Ethan Roberts, a boy traumatized by a murder he witnessed as a kid, who has been working for the Guard to protect history for years now, and Isabel, a magically gifted girl (whose brother's best friend Ethan used to be before their epic falling out) that Ethan is tasked to train to become a guardian. I really like both of them, and I also love the side characters (some of whom are narrators in the next two books!). I also love the friendships in this story, and though I'm not a big fan of insta-love (which is very, very real in this book), there are some interesting romantic relationships going on and set up in the Named.<br /><br />I've read this book and its sequels so many times in my life that I know them super well, but they never get old. I'm always invested, amused and emotionally connected to the characters. Can't wait to continue my thousandth re-read and pick up the Dark!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11251340234963535211" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6157894315700325610">It was a bit odd at first... i felt rushed into the whole excitement and worried that it would get worse. The beginning was off-putting but it quickly saved itself. The beginning was quite predictable but once i felt like i knew the whole book it flipped in a matter of seconds.   <span id="freeText6157894315700325610" style="display:none">It was a bit odd at first... i felt rushed into the whole excitement and worried that it would get worse. The beginning was off-putting but it quickly saved itself. The beginning was quite predictable but once i felt like i knew the whole book it flipped in a matter of seconds. It has a great story and i'm excited to see what else will be done with the idea. I do love how everything is far from perfect and characters are tested and its just all really great. I hope it only gets better from here<br /><br />I'm coming back to this and i'm going to say that it definitely wasnt perfect. It could've been better with more backround on the characters. And certain things were just... added in to help with the story, but i'm hoping the next book will take you deeper into this world of new things. I want to know more about arkarian and more about there journeys into the past. i want to know more of the guard and what they are doing. But this book was very enjoyable for me to read at home sick. And i really do recomend it even if just for a short read.<br /><br />It could have gone deeper into characters, but i'm hoping much more will be revealed about them in the next book, and i'm pretty happy with what i knew about the characters. I'm glad some things happened that i wasnt able to predict but i'm also glad characters stuck to who they were and didnt do random things that didnt fit their persona just to advance the plot. So overall this book was really well done in my opinion, but maybe i'm just easy to please.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer663189307232133225">I liked the concept, and the historical element was fun. <br/>The characters were interesting, and I especially liked Arkarian, Isabel and Ethan, in that order.<br/><br/>However, I felt the prose seemed to be aimed at a younger audience, and it would go from being very simplistic to extremely intricate plot devices at the drop of a hat.   <span id="freeText663189307232133225" style="display:none">I liked the concept, and the historical element was fun. <br />The characters were interesting, and I especially liked Arkarian, Isabel and Ethan, in that order.<br /><br />However, I felt the prose seemed to be aimed at a younger audience, and it would go from being very simplistic to extremely intricate plot devices at the drop of a hat. The imagery was good, but sometimes I felt lost rather than in the moment. <br /><br />Also, everyone has a soul-mate, and they're all conveniently going to find each other. <br />Hmm.<br /><br />I just wasn't in the mood for young love, so it kind of ticked me off, but other than that it was an enjoyable read. <br />I won't be continuing on with the series, but I can see how it would appeal to others.<br />I'm interested ti see how it turns out, actually.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11224332222364373088">This book was just okay for me. The basic premise--guarding history through going back in time and thwarting attempts to change it--was interesting, but the motives of those seeking to change history were not believable, and the characters seemed superficial. Absent of any surprises and turns, the plot was predictable. All in all it was a pleasant read but that is similar to labeling one's new hairstyle "different" or "interesting".</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YzAWSEIvDR3rZX/aEEHP4D/ztVYSgd7s0SZeqzW5z7a0QvgUk2LOXQoEyxewqYxv+CW6KvQFMJtJWbMctQYyQw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VH5dG5QabaAlLeje9bBpe30mwi4phzo03RhArTxmGh2DDLNHRVeu4MRMXBNVWCr0uvDNUs8D1ENFZ60avNnn6A==')})
  }
//]]>

Instead, after a year and a half of nea<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText115124064044932603\" style=\"display:none\">Adapted for young people from the New York Times best-seller In the Heart of the Sea.\n\nIn 1819, the Essex, a Nantucket whaleship carrying a crew of 20, began what all thought would be a normal, two-year voyage. Instead, after a year and a half of near-disasters, the ship was rammed by a sperm whale and sank in the Pacific. All hands got off in three whaleboats and were at sea for three unbearable months of short rations and little fresh water, leading to the death by starvation of some and the killing of others to provide food. One boat disappeared and the two remaining eventually became separated. When rescued off the coast of Chile, only five men were still alive, including the captain and first mate, as well as three rescued later from an island. Philbrick brings the era to life, giving readers a rounded picture of the whaling industry and its society. Relying mainly on two survivors\' detailed accounts, one of which has just recently been found, he fleshes out the tale in an exciting manner that sweeps readers along. He includes modern medical knowledge of the physical and mental effects of starvation on humans. The book concludes with tales of other shipwrecks, a description of how the survivors lived the rest of their lives, and an introduction to the recent work of the Nantucket Whaling Museum. The contrast between today\'s touristy island paradise and yesterday\'s hard life will not be lost on teens.\n\n—Judy McAloon, Potomac Library, Prince William County, VA<\/span>\n  <a Since then the color divide has become a symbol of a culture war that thrives on stereotypes--pickup-driving red-state Republicans who vote based on God, guns, and gays; and elitist, latte-sipping blue-state Democrats who are woefully out of touch with heartland values. Red State, Blue State, Rich State, Poor State debunks these and other political myths.\n\nWith wit and prodigious number crunching, Andrew Gelman gets to the bottom of why Democrats win elections in wealthy states while Republicans get the votes of richer voters, how the two parties have become ideologically polarized, and other issues. Gelman uses eye-opening, easy-to-read graphics to unravel the mystifying patterns of recent voting, and in doing so paints a vivid portrait of the regional differences that drive American politics. He demonstrates in the plainest possible terms how the real culture war is being waged among affluent Democrats and Republicans, not between the haves and have-nots; how religion matters for higher-income voters; how the rich-poor divide is greater in red not blue states--and much more.\n\nRed State, Blue State, Rich State, Poor State is a must-read for anyone seeking to make sense of today\'s fractured American political landscape.\n\nMyths and facts about the red and the blue:\n\nMyth The rich vote based on economics, the poor vote &quot;God, guns, and gays.&quot;Fact Church attendance predicts Republican voting much more among rich than poor.\n\nMyth A political divide exists between working-class &quot;red America&quot; and rich &quot;blue America.&quot;Fact Within any state, more rich people vote Republican. The real divide is between higher-income voters in red and blue states.\n\nMyth Rich people vote for the Democrats.Fact George W. Bush won more than 60 percent of high-income voters.\n\nMyth Religion is particularly divisive in American politics.Fact Religious and secular voters differ no more in America than in France, Germany, <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14819079795631334842">I loved reading from a young age and scoured my school libraries during my younger years, but I never thought I would become a writer. It was not until my mid-thirties, while teaching office studies and computers to adults at the Coffs Harbour Education Campus that I began to think seriously about writing. I took several courses and experimented with different styles and genres. With two teenage d</span>
  <span id="freeText14819079795631334842" style="display:none">I loved reading from a young age and scoured my school libraries during my younger years, but I never thought I would become a writer. It was not until my mid-thirties, while teaching office studies and computers to adults at the Coffs Harbour Education Campus that I began to think seriously about writing. I took several courses and experimented with different styles and genres. With two teenage daughters at the time I fell into writing young adult paranormal and have never looked back.<br /> <br />My first four novels, Old Magic, The Named, The Dark and The Key, were published by Bloomsbury Publishing in Australia, the UK, and the USA, with translations into more than a dozen foreign languages. <br /><br />In 2004, just as The Key was being prepared for printing, I was diagnosed with an aggressive form of bone marrow cancer called Myelofibrosis. With only a short time to live, I was given a stem-cell bone marrow transplant using my sister’s cells, which saved my life. I have now been cancer free for fourteen years and have written a new trilogy called The Avena Series. All three books - Hidden, Broken and Fearless were published between 2013 and 2015. <br /><br />My latest book is The Shadow, the long-awaited and much anticipated fourth book in The Guardians of Time Series. The Shadow will be released in March 2018. <br /><br />I am presently working on a YA paranormal/time travel story, and a contemporary novel based on real events. <br /><br />Website: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://mariannecurley7.com">http://mariannecurley7.com</a> <br />Email: marianne.curley7@gmail.com<br />Facebook: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/marianne.curley.75">https://www.facebook.com/marianne.cur...</a><br />Facebook Author: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/MarianneCurleyAuthor">https://www.facebook.com/MarianneCurl...</a><br />Insta: @marianne_curley</span>
